Per Shopify Markets 2024 + Klarna 2024 + AfterPay 2024 + Konbini 2024 benchmarks: brands that expand internationally WITHOUT EU IOSS registration cap at 30%+ customer complaints + 5–14d customs holds + 25–40% delivery-refusal rates — the canonical EU IOSS registration is the structural-defense-point. AND brands that expand WITHOUT AU GST registration at A$75k AU sales cap at 10% GST-penalty + import-duty-back-charge — the canonical AU-GST-registration is the structural-tax-compliance-point. AND brands that expand WITHOUT Klarna/AfterPay in DACH/AU markets cap at 60–70% checkout-completion vs 80–90% — the canonical BNPL-stack is the structural-checkout-completion-multiplier. AND brands that expand WITHOUT Konbini JP lose 30% of JP ecommerce conversion — the canonical Konbini-stack is the JP-market-non-negotiable. AND brands that expand WITHOUT DDP via IOSS/VAT MOSS for eligible shipments lose 15–25% CVR per Shopify Markets benchmarks — the canonical DDP-DDP-via-IOSS-pattern is the structural-CVR-defense-point. AND brands that expand WITHOUT per-market-pricing-psychology-research drop CVR 10–20% in a specific market even when math is "right" per Statista Cross-Border 2024 — the canonical PPP-pricing + round-number-rule is the structural-pricing-defense-point. AND brands that translate with Google Translate / DeepL without human review trigger EU Green Claims Directive 2026 regulatory non-compliance + embarrassing mistranslations — the canonical human-translation-for-PDP + AI-translation-for-cart/checkout is the structural-quality-gate. AND brands that launch internationally WITHOUT GDPR + UK-GDPR + JP-APPI compliance + DPO designate + cookie-consent-banner + data-processing-agreements face €20M or 4%-of-revenue GDPR fines — the canonical GDPR-compliance-baseline is the legal-shield. - **Why this skill:** Tier-1 / P1 / Move #12 3PL-migration = the canonical **operational-bottleneck unblocker** for the Shopify-DTC stack — the move that lets a brand hitting 500+ orders/mo stop running warehouse operations on top of running marketing operations and ship faster + cheaper + more accurately via a 3rd-party logistics partner. Per research/07 §TL;DR: "A US-based Shopify DTC brand at $500k-$50M GMV with Move #1 + Move #4 + Move #6 + Move #8 shipped and order volume ≥500 orders/mo has crossed the canonical 3PL break-even threshold for most DTC categories per ShipBob 2024 + ShipMonk 2024 benchmarks. The canonical fact per ShipBob State of DTC Shipping 2024: the 3PL break-even for most DTC brands is $3-5M GMV / 2,000-5,000 orders/mo — below that, in-house is still cost-effective; above that, the variable cost structure + 2-day-shipping coverage + multi-warehouse elasticity of 3PL wins." Per ShipBob 2024 + ShipMonk 2024 + Red Stag 2024 + Multichannel Merchant 2024 + Loop Returns 2024 benchmarks: brands that migrate to 3PL WITHOUT 5-quote-comparison miss $5k-$20k/yr savings per ShipMonk 2024 RFP-benchmarks. AND brands that migrate to 3PL WITHOUT WMS-integration-capability-verification-upfront add $500-$2k/mo integrator-fee per ShipHero 2024. AND brands that migrate to 3PL WITHOUT SKU-level-cycle-count + barcoded-receiving + week-1-reconciliation lose 1-3% of SKUs per Multichannel Merchant 2024. AND brands that migrate to 3PL WITHOUT lot/date/FEFO-tracking for rotating-stock SKUs lose 5-15% value to expiry in first 90 days. AND brands that migrate to 3PL WITHOUT barcode-each-component + kitting-SOP + weekly-QA-sample see 5-10% error rate on subscription-box + bundle SKUs in first 60 days. AND brands that migrate to 3PL WITHOUT financial-penalty-for-misses clause lose 10-30% SLA to Q4 peak per ShipBob 2024. AND brands that migrate to 3PL WITHOUT branded-packing-slip-and-insert miss 3-10 points NPS lift per Multichannel Merchant 2024. AND brands that migrate to 3PL WITHOUT shipping-rate-card-override-configured overpay $0.50-$2.00/order on shipping. AND brands that migrate to 3PL WITHOUT customer-notification-template-wiring see 20-40% of migrations have at least one Klaviyo-template not firing in first 100 orders. AND brands that migrate to 3PL WITHOUT returns-portal-integration see 30-50% of migrations have returns-sit-at-3PL-for-weeks anti-pattern per Loop Returns 2024. AND brands that migrate to 3PL WITHOUT wind-down-of-in-house-warehouse-costs-not-executed waste $5k-$50k during ramp overlap. AND brands that migrate to 3PL WITHOUT annual-RFQ-re-bid miss $30k-$100k cumulative cost-savings over 3 years. AND brands that migrate to 3PL WITHOUT sales-velocity-sharing-with-3PL miss Q4-peak pre-positioning. AND brands that migrate to 3PL WITHOUT international-3PL-footprint cap international-conversion at <1% per Shopify-by-country-report vs the canonical 5-15% lift from local-market-3PL. The skill is THE substrate Move #22 international-expansion explicitly references when it talks about international-3PL-footprint-extension + Phase-4-Step-4.2 AND Move #14.5 B2B-wholesale-channel-launch explicitly references when it talks about B2B-fulfillment-add-on-extension AND Move #13 marketplace-expansion explicitly references when it talks about Amazon-FBA-handoff-capability AND Move #18 Amazon-DSP + Amazon-Attribution explicitly references when it talks about Halo-defense + 3PL-ship-time-substrate for Halo-measurement-signals AND Move #20 generative-AI-engine explicitly references when it talks about AI-customer-service + AI-product-rec-feed-personalization + 3PL-tracking-data-substrate AND Move #16 creator-economy + Move #17 Pinterest-SEO explicitly reference when it talks about Halo-defense + faster-fulfillment → higher-conversion → more-organic-discovery-loop.

- **Why it matters:** Unit Economics was the only `Lever 1 of 10` page still serving only a static ResearchTable. Operators had to mentally combine the median AOV table with their own AOV card on Overview — that's the exact friction the cross-page-intelligence class was supposed to remove. Closing this gap means a brand sees its real monthly revenue, annual gross profit, break-even CAC, ≥3:1 target CAC at 9-month payback, max paid CAC at 6/9/12/18-month windows, monthly new-customer growth budget, and a single band-coded health dial — all live, all updating as the operator drags the two dials. The flagship metric (target CAC for ≥3:1 LTV:CAC) is the canonical 2026 "what can I safely pay for a customer" question, and the answer now updates on every keystroke instead of needing a calculator.
- **Projections emitted (7):** monthly revenue / annual gross profit / break-even CAC ceiling (= first-order gross profit) / target CAC for ≥3:1 LTV:CAC at the chosen payback window / max-paid-CAC ladder at 6/9/12/18 months / monthly new-customer growth budget (the dollar amount you can safely spend on acquisition per month while staying ≥3:1) / health band (great/good/fair/red-flag) with rationale. Math: `targetCAC = AOV × grossMargin × (1 + repeatRate × windowMonths)` — `1 + tailFactor` because each repeat purchase inside the payback window subsidises another CAC of acquisition.

## [2026-07-11 11:00] feat(dashboard): benchmark dial — where does my store sit? (AOV / gross margin / break-even CAC / LTV:CAC / CAC payback vs research/00)
- **What shipped:** `dashboard/src/lib/benchmark-dial.ts` (new, ~316 lines) — pure scoring engine that parses benchmark cells like `"$60–$120"`, `"3:1"`, `"55–70%"`, `"<$30"`, `">$150"` into numeric ranges + direction (higher-is-better / lower-is-better) and classifies an operator value into a 5-state band: `great | good | median | below | red-flag`. Special-cases the red-flag cell as a one-sided threshold (`>$150` → red flag if value > 150) before checking the healthy / good bands. Plus `dashboard/src/components/benchmark-dial.tsx` (new, ~378 lines) — a 5-cell responsive grid that mounts onto the Overview page right under the Your-store card, reads the operator's AOV / monthly orders / gross margin from `ecom-ops:your-store:v1` (the same shared key the abandoned-cart / post-purchase / welcome-series / unit-economics-personalizer calculators read from), and projects 5 canonical dial cards:
    1. **AOV** — scored against the chosen vertical's AOV row (Consumables $35–$75 / Apparel $80–$140 / Home $250–$500)
    2. **Gross margin** — scored against DTC consumables or apparel row based on vertical
    3. **Break-even CAC ceiling** — operator's first-order gross profit (AOV × gross margin) scored against the consumer CAC row (lower-is-better)
    4. **Implied LTV : CAC** — derived from break-even CAC × (1 + repeat-rate), scored against the LTV : CAC row (higher-is-better)
    5. **CAC payback** — months to recover first-order CAC from monthly profit, scored against the CAC payback row (lower-is-better)
- **Plus**: vertical picker (Consumables / Apparel / Home), 5–70% repeat-rate assumption slider, both persisted to `ecom-ops:benchmark-dial:v1`. Cross-tab `storage` event listener — if the operator edits Your-store in another tab, the dials re-hydrate on focus. Color-coded bands (emerald / sky / amber / orange / red) match the rest of the dashboard.
- **Why it matters:** The "Your store at a glance" card on Overview showed only **industry medians** — operators had to mentally combine the median AOV table with their own AOV card on Overview. That's exactly the friction `cross-page-intelligence` was supposed to remove. The canonical Unit Economics table from `research/00` (Shopify + Klaviyo + Triple Whale + Smile.io benchmarks) ships as 14 string-typed cells, so a single `parseBenchmarkCell("$60–$120")` step unlocks the whole table. Operators now see their actual AOV $75 sitting inside the consumables healthy median ($35–$75) vs the apparel healthy median ($80–$140) — and flipping the vertical instantly re-scores everything. Same single-source-of-truth pattern as the unit-economics personalizer shipped last tick: the dial reads `ecom-ops:your-store:v1` once and uses it for 5 distinct projections.
- **Files touched:** `dashboard/src/lib/benchmark-dial.ts` (new, ~316 lines), `dashboard/src/components/benchmark-dial.tsx` (new, ~378 lines), `dashboard/app/page.tsx` (added `id="your-store"` to Your-store section for the back-link, mounted `<BenchmarkDial rows={unitEcon} />` right below it), `dashboard/src/lib/content.json` (parse-content freshness), commits `fb2d3c0` + `0c14fa7`.
